## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on restoring forces (functions of x), dissipative forces (functions of v), and possibly external driving (functions of t). The nonlinearity can appear in the restoring force, damping, or both.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodic external driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic-cubic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric potential)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * (x**2 + v**2) (amplitude-dependent damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Mathieu-type: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (parametric excitation)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 * v + c2 * v (Rayleigh-Duffing type)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential well preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power position terms (x²) → asymmetric potential indicating broken reflection symmetry
- Velocity terms proportional to (1 - x²)·v → self-sustained oscillation with amplitude-dependent damping (limit cycles)
- Cosine/sine of (c·t) as additive terms → external periodic driving force at frequency c
- Product of position powers and velocity (x²·v) → nonlinear damping that depends on displacement amplitude
- Negative coefficient on x with positive coefficient on x³ → double-well potential (bistability)
- Odd functions of velocity (v, v³) → dissipation preserving time-reversal antisymmetry of damping
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous/conservative system where energy analysis applies
- Rational functions of x like x/(1 + c·x²) → bounded restoring force modeling physical saturation of spring stiffness

**GT:** `-1.02670587028003*x**3 - 1.02670587028003*x*exp(-Abs(x)) + 0.947981592038046*sin(t) - 0.712276797350088*sin(v)`

Key components of GT:

2. `x*exp(-|x|)` term with coefficient ≈ -1.027
3. `sin(t)` term with coefficient ≈ 0.948
4. `sin(v)` (not `v`) term with coefficient ≈ -0.712

**Critical observation:** The GT has `-beta*sin(v)`, which is a **sin(v)** term. Most candidates have terms like `v`, `v**3`, `v/(v²+1)`, or `v*|v|` — none of these equal `sin(v)`.

The Taylor series of sin(v) = v - v³/6 + v⁵/120 - ... So candidates with polynomial terms in v (like `c*v + c*v**3`) can only approximate sin(v), not match it exactly for all v.

Similarly, `v/(c*v²+1)` is a rational function, not sin(v).

The GT also has `x*exp(-|x|)`. Most candidates don't have this term. Some have `x*exp(c*x²)` — but `exp(c*x²)` ≠ `exp(-|x|)` for any constant c, since one is a function of x² in the exponent and the other has |x|.

Let me check candidates with `x*exp(c*x²)` terms: candidates 1, 2, 4, 8 (no exp), 10, 41, 45.

For `x*exp(c*x²)` to equal `x*exp(-|x|)`, we'd need `c*x² = -|x|` for all x, which is impossible.

Some candidates have `x*log(c*x²+1)` (candidate 22, 44) — also cannot match `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Now, could the `x*exp(-|x|)` term be absorbed by polynomial/rational terms? The function `x*exp(-|x|)` is not a polynomial or rational function, so no finite combination of polynomial and rational terms can reproduce it exactly.

Let me check if any candidate has a term structure that could produce both `sin(v)` AND `x*exp(-|x|)`:

- `sin(v)` needs to come from somewhere. Only candidate 7 has a `sin()` function, but it's `sin(c4*x + c5)`, which depends on x, not v.
- `cos(c+t)` with appropriate c gives `sin(t)` (since cos(t - π/2) = sin(t)), so that's fine for the t-dependence.

**No candidate has a `sin(v)` term.** The v-dependence in GT is `sin(v)`, which cannot be exactly represented by `v`, `v**3`, `v/(v²+1)`, `v*|v|`, or any polynomial/rational function of v.

Also, **no candidate has `exp(-|x|)` or anything equivalent.** The `exp(c*x²)` terms cannot match `exp(-|x|)`.

Therefore, no candidate can be made mathematically equivalent to the GT.

Let me double-check candidates with both `v/(c*v²+1)` and `x*exp(c*x²)` (candidates 1, 4, 10, 41) — even these can't work because:
- `v/(c*v²+1)` ≠ `sin(v)` for all v
- `x*exp(c*x²)` ≠ `x*exp(-|x|)` for all x

No candidate can match the GT.
